Hi, 

You need to use the Python executable created by crest (not the system Python) when running any crest tools (see https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/docs/development.md#setting-up-a-virtualenv for more details). 
This python is created in the bin/ subdirectory. 

Ellie

From Eleanor.Merry at metaswitch.com  Fri Jul 17 08:00:02 2015
From: Eleanor.Merry at metaswitch.com (Eleanor Merry)
Date: Fri, 17 Jul 2015 12:00:02 +0000
Subject: [Clearwater] homestead bulk provisioning issue
In-Reply-To: <55A8D488.7010302@cse.iitb.ac.in>
References: <55A652C5.8000405@cse.iitb.ac.in>
	<CO1PR02MB2403DC4FBE7FF706AA6A3F89B990@CO1PR02MB240.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>
	<55A8D488.7010302@cse.iitb.ac.in>
Message-ID: <CO1PR02MB24014C95CB6C021AE87060B9B980@CO1PR02MB240.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi Priyanka, 

You shouldn't need to set XDMS_HOSTNAME in local_settings.py for Homestead-prov. You will need to set the XDM_DEFAULT_SIMSERVS_FILE, you can do this by adding the following to your local_settings.py file (note the quotes):

XDM_DEFAULT_SIMSERVS_FILE = "/usr/share/clearwater/homestead/modules/common/metaswitch/common/default_simservs.xml" 

You can see an example of Homestead-prov's local_settings file at https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/homestead.local_settings/local_settings.py 

Ellie

From Robert.Day at metaswitch.com  Wed Jul 22 06:04:47 2015
From: Robert.Day at metaswitch.com (Robert Day)
Date: Wed, 22 Jul 2015 10:04:47 +0000
Subject: [Clearwater] Jane Eyre release note
Message-ID: <BN3PR0201MB0948F6EA54B87D0839AAE38DF4830@BN3PR0201MB0948.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

The release for sprint "Jane Eyre" has been cut.  The code for this release is tagged as release-77 in Github.

The main new feature in this release is the addition of registration and authentication-related statistics, as described at http://clearwater.readthedocs.org/en/latest/Clearwater_SNMP_Statistics/index.html. We've also enhanced Cacti to graph them - see http://clearwater.readthedocs.org/en/latest/Cacti/index.html for instructions and our Cacti templates.

This release includes the following bug fixes:


*         Sprout crashes during long traffic runs with a VoLTE TAS (4) (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1108)

*         Sprout crashes during long traffic runs with a VoLTE TAS (3) (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1107)

*         Sprout crashes during long traffic runs with a VoLTE TAS (2) (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1106)

*         Sprout crashes during long traffic runs with a VoLTE TAS (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1105)

*         Sprout crashing at low call rate with VoLTE TAS (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1095)

*         Sprout stops responding to SIP requests at high traffic load when configured with a CFS TAS, scenario 2.  (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/1088)

*         Sprout crash at high traffic load when configured with a CFS TAS. (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/981)

*         Sprout stops responding to SIP requests at high traffic load when configured with a CFS TAS. (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/980)

*         sprout requires P-CSCF to specify a Path header (https://github.com/Metaswitch/sprout/issues/639)

*         Homestead  and homestead-prov still use the "preferred" flag (https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead/issues/43)

*         Ralf doesn't produce any alarms relating to communication with chronos or memcached (https://github.com/Metaswitch/ralf/issues/119)

*         POSTs and PUTs from HttpConnection have wrong Content-Type (https://github.com/Metaswitch/cpp-common/issues/336)

*         HTTPConnection doesn't use the HTTP SAS compression profile (https://github.com/Metaswitch/cpp-common/issues/335)

*         Portions of BYE transactions split into multiple SAS traces. (https://github.com/Metaswitch/cpp-common/issues/310)

*         SAS call flows are sometimes drawn with out of order events. (https://github.com/Metaswitch/cpp-common/issues/309)

*         We no longer support multiple IP addresses in snmp_ip (https://github.com/Metaswitch/clearwater-snmp-handlers/issues/70)

*         Alarms issued from C++ not being reported (https://github.com/Metaswitch/clearwater-snmp-handlers/issues/36)

If you are deploying an all-in-one node, the standard image (http://vm-images.cw-ngv.com/cw-aio.ova) has been updated for this release.

Thanks,
Rob

--
Rob Day
Software Engineer, Project Clearwater

METASWITCH NETWORKS
THE BRAINS OF THE NEW GLOBAL NETWORK
www.metaswitch.com<http://www.metaswitch.com/>

From Eleanor.Merry at metaswitch.com  Wed Jul 22 13:15:01 2015
From: Eleanor.Merry at metaswitch.com (Eleanor Merry)
Date: Wed, 22 Jul 2015 17:15:01 +0000
Subject: [Clearwater] sprout cannot connect to homestead
In-Reply-To: <55ACF191.9050600@cse.iitb.ac.in>
References: <55ACF191.9050600@cse.iitb.ac.in>
Message-ID: <CO1PR02MB240C96B4F3D5146DE18D90F9B830@CO1PR02MB240.namprd02.prod.outlook.com>

Hi Priyanka, 

It looks like you're only running Homestead-prov (https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/docs/homestead_prov_features.md), not Homestead itself (https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead/blob/dev/docs/homestead_overview.md). 

Homestead-prov is the provisioning interface to Homestead; it provides a restful HTTP interface for creating/deleting/querying subscribers. It is the Homestead process that is the HSS-cache (and so what Sprout connects to). 

You can find the Homestead code at https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead, and development details at https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead/blob/dev/docs/development.md. You should collocate your Homestead and Homestead-prov processes (so they use the same underlying Cassandra database). 

To delete all numbers on Homestead, run the following:

cqlsh

USE homestead_provisioning;
TRUNCATE public;
TRUNCATE private;
TRUNCATE service_profiles;
TRUNCATE implicit_registration_sets;

USE homestead_cache;
TRUNCATE impi;
TRUNCATE impu;
TRUNCATE impi_mapping;

To delete all numbers on Homer, run the following:

cqlsh

USE homer;
TRUNCATE simservs;

Ellie

Hi David,

Do you want to keep any information on the deployment (e.g. subscribers)? You can resize the deployment to have a minimal number of nodes (1 each of Ellis, Sprout, Homer, Homestead) if you don??t need the full capacity of your current deployment.

Otherwise, we typically just delete the deployments when not in use (knife deployment delete ?CE <env name>), and then just recreate it the next time we need it (knife deployment resize ?CE <env name>).

Ellie

Hi David,

Can you try resetting the validator key and retrying?

You can do this through the chef server web UI by going to Policy->Clients, selecting the alu-validator client, then selecting the reset option in the details section. You??ll need to do it this way rather than through the Administration tab, as it appears this links to the wrong key. Can you then copy the new private key to your chef client and retry?

Ellie

From: Eleanor Merry [mailto:Eleanor.Merry at metaswitch.com]

To: LIN David DL; clearwater at lists.projectclearwater.org<mailto:clearwater at lists.projectclearwater.org>
Subject: RE: Problems encountered when installing Clearwater on AWS EC2

Hi David,

If you??ve created the instances through chef, but terminated them through AWS, then this leaves the chef client in a bad state and it can??t create any new instances. You??ll need to delete the instances in chef as well to be able to move on.
You can do this by logging onto the chef server web UI as the admin user, and then deleting any nodes you??ve created from the Nodes tab and the Clients tab.

You??ll then be able to create a new deployment. If this fails again, can you please send me the logs? The location of the logs is shown when the instance is being created, e.g.:

Waiting for server...INFO: Bootstrapping clearwater-ralf-1, logs can be found at /home/ubuntu/chef/plugins/knife/../../logs/clearwater-ralf-1-bootstrap-1429769747.log

Ellie

Hi David,

If you??ve created the instances through chef, but terminated them through AWS, then this leaves the chef client in a bad state and it can??t create any new instances. You??ll need to delete the instances in chef as well to be able to move on.
You can do this by logging onto the chef server web UI as the admin user, and then deleting any nodes you??ve created from the Nodes tab and the Clients tab.

You??ll then be able to create a new deployment. If this fails again, can you please send me the logs? The location of the logs is shown when the instance is being created, e.g.:

Waiting for server...INFO: Bootstrapping clearwater-ralf-1, logs can be found at /home/ubuntu/chef/plugins/knife/../../logs/clearwater-ralf-1-bootstrap-1429769747.log

Hi Priyanka,

That's correct. You can run homestead interactively using 'LD_LIBRARY_PATH=usr/lib:$LD_LIBRARY_PATH build/bin/homestead' in the top level Homestead directory. You can see what parameters are available by passing '-h', and you can find out more information about these options at http://clearwater.readthedocs.org/en/latest/Clearwater_Configuration_Options_Reference/index.html.

What are you using Clearwater for? You can also just install Clearwater from debian packages - see http://clearwater.readthedocs.org/en/latest/Manual_Install/index.html for more details.

Ellie

From: Clearwater [mailto:clearwater-bounces at lists.projectclearwater.org] On Behalf Of Priyanka

To: clearwater at lists.projectclearwater.org
Subject: Re: [Clearwater] sprout cannot connect to homestead

Priyanka

On Wednesday 22 July 2015 10:45 PM, Eleanor Merry wrote:

Hi Priyanka,



It looks like you're only running Homestead-prov (https://github.com/Metaswitch/crest/blob/dev/docs/homestead_prov_features.md), not Homestead itself (https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead/blob/dev/docs/homestead_overview.md).



Homestead-prov is the provisioning interface to Homestead; it provides a restful HTTP interface for creating/deleting/querying subscribers. It is the Homestead process that is the HSS-cache (and so what Sprout connects to).



You can find the Homestead code at https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead, and development details at https://github.com/Metaswitch/homestead/blob/dev/docs/development.md. You should collocate your Homestead and Homestead-prov processes (so they use the same underlying Cassandra database).



To delete all numbers on Homestead, run the following:



cqlsh



USE homestead_provisioning;

TRUNCATE public;

TRUNCATE private;

TRUNCATE service_profiles;

TRUNCATE implicit_registration_sets;



USE homestead_cache;

TRUNCATE impi;

TRUNCATE impu;

TRUNCATE impi_mapping;



To delete all numbers on Homer, run the following:



cqlsh



USE homer;

TRUNCATE simservs;



Ellie

Hi John,

We don?t actually support this. The RFC suggests that on a TCP connection the client should send a keep-alive as a double CRLF, and the server should respond with a single CRLF.

I?ll update our supported RFCs page.

Ellie

Hi,

You need to set the auth. Username in Zoiper to be the private identity of the subscriber - so something like 65055550595@<domain>.

It also looks like there's some issues with Chronos (our timer service - see https://github.com/Metaswitch/chronos/blob/dev/doc/technical.md for more details). Can you please send me your Chronos logs (in /var/log/chronos) and configuration (in /etc/chronos)?

Thanks,
Ellie

From peter.skrzynski at nec.co.nz  Fri Jul 31 00:40:50 2015
From: peter.skrzynski at nec.co.nz (Peter Skrzynski)
Date: Fri, 31 Jul 2015 04:40:50 +0000
Subject: [Clearwater] Clearwater multiple netwrok support.
Message-ID: <CF1D25D9B4A39245B959CAA35549B9DC013E931244@necexc01v.necnz.internal>

Hello,
I have a manual install of bono/sprout/homestead/ibcf/dns being used as an interface between Voip UE?s and a PSTN, running on 5 VM?s. They are connected via a private virtual switch, and only the bono and ibcf nodes are connected to an external network interface for external sip signalling. This setup is working with no problems.
However, I wanted to try and implement ?multiple network support? to separate the internal management and traffic signalling. I followed the instructions on the readthedocs page, adding another external network interface to each node. All nodes can ping each other via this new interface (ip netns exec signalling ping 10.10.10.x). So now bono and ibcf have 3 network interfaces, however  the bono and ibcf nodes do not stand up. Other nodes stand up OK.
It is a bit confusing that the ?manual install? page talks about having separate private_IP and public_IP interfaces, but then the ?multiple network support? page talks about adding a second interface, when we already have a second interface. I assume this is to provide the security of a separate namespace?
I am using 10.10.10.x for internal signalling, 192.168.10.x for internal management and acbd.xyz.co.nz for domain, and my public network side is 172.20.99.x.

The bono log files show the following failure point (cannot start port 5060)?
30-07-2015 04:56:00.334 UTC Verbose pjsip:   udp0x1e17f70 SIP UDP transport started, published address is 10.10.10.10:5058
30-07-2015 04:56:00.334 UTC Verbose pjsip:    tcplis:5058 SIP TCP listener ready for incoming connections at 10.10.10.10:5058
30-07-2015 04:56:00.334 UTC Status stack.cpp:373: Listening on port 5058
30-07-2015 04:56:00.334 UTC Verbose pjsip:   udp0x218a550 SIP UDP transport started, published address is abcd.xyz.co.nz:5060
30-07-2015 04:56:00.335 UTC Error stack.cpp:343: Failed to start TCP transport for port 5060 (Invalid value or argument (PJ_EINVAL))
30-07-2015 04:56:00.335 UTC Error pjsip: Assert failed: stack.cpp:707 status == 0
30-07-2015 04:56:00.334 UTC Error main.cpp:1645: Error initializing stack Invalid value or argument (PJ_EINVAL)

Is it even possible for a bono node to use 3 network interfaces? (one for external SIP, one for internal management and one for internal signalling).
Or do I just have a problem with my dns/network/iptables setup?
Or Clearwater config file? (as follows?)
Or do I need to specify management side of 192.168.10.x somewhere in the config file?

home_domain=abcd.xyz.co.nz
sprout_hostname=sprout.abcd.xyz.co.nz
chronos_hostname=localhost:7253
hs_hostname-hs.abcd.xyz.co.nz:8888
hs_provisioning_hostname=hs.abcd.xyz.co.nz:8889
signalling_namespace=signalling
signalling_dns_server=10.10.10.1
local_ip=10.10.10.10
public_id=172.20.99.233
public_hostname=abcd.xyz.co.nz

Regards, Peter.
